We could actually build schools to help these kids train for free and be self- sustainable and give them an opportunity to aspire to something. And that's why it's live and free on YouTube. They can look up and say, "Hey, maybe that could be me one day on stage." But, you know, jiu-jitsu fills a lot of voids in life. And I feel like giving someone the opportunity to have a space to train for free, it helps grow the sport because the more kids that are in the sport, the more family support, that means the community is growing, the sport of jiu-jitsu is growing, and that elevates the entire sport, not just professional athletes, but jiu-jitsu as a whole. Let's remind you of the rules real quick and then we'll get going. Let's go ahead. Here's the rules. The Craig Jones Invitational is back with a brand new take on team grappling in partnership with Quintet and the Japanese grappling pioneer Kazushi Sakuraba. CJI will feature a special team duel format. Five on five. Winner stays on. Victory is earned by eliminating your opponents one by one. The action takes place in the CJI pit. Each team has five members at different weights. 66 kg, 77 kg, 88 kg, 99 kg, and plus 99 kg. The action starts when the coaches call out their first athletes. Every match is 8 minutes long, regardless of the weight difference. There are no points and elimination occurs when an athlete submits their opponent. All submissions are legal. Chokes, arm, leg, and joint blocks. Slamming is only allowed to escape a locked on submission. The winning athlete stays on to compete against the next opponent and could potentially face all five members of the rival team. In the case of a draw, both competitors are eliminated and will leave the pit. The special CGI twist is that nobody knows which matches will happen until the competitors step into the arena. The coaches call out their next competitor at the end of each match and can strategically choose their athlete based on the opponent waiting in the pit. Whichever team eliminates their opponents first will win the duel. If the team duel ends with five double eliminations, the judges will decide the winner with an aggregate tally of the matches. There is no open scoring. The referees will keep the action going by issuing penalties for inactivity, stalling, or trying to flee the pit. Whichever team finishes off their last fighter is the winner and will move on in the tournament as they look to take home the $1 million cash prize.
